# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Scheduler Framework Plugin Extension Points

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that define the scheduler framework plugin extension points: the PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, and PostBind interfaces and their registration in the scheduler framework.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully created the `/workspace/answer.json` file with comprehensive information about the Kubernetes scheduler framework plugin extension points. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've identified all the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that define the scheduler framework plugin extension points:

### **Core Extension Point Interfaces** (9 interfaces)
Located in `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/interface.go`:
1. **PreFilterPlugin** - Runs at the beginning of the scheduling cycle
2. **FilterPlugin** - Filters out nodes that cannot run a pod
3. **PostFilterPlugin** - Runs after filtering fails
4. **PreScorePlugin** - Informational phase before scoring
5. **ScorePlugin** - Ranks nodes that passed filtering
6. **ReservePlugin** - Updates plugin state after node assignment
7. **PreBindPlugin** - Runs before pod binding
8. **BindPlugin** - Binds pod to a node
9. **PostBindPlugin** - Runs after successful binding
10. **PermitPlugin** - Controls/delays pod binding

### **Supporting Infrastructure**
- **Framework Implementation** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`): Contains the `frameworkImpl` struct and all `Run*` methods that execute plugins at each extension point
- **Plugin Registry** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go`): Manages plugin registration via the `Registry` type
- **Configuration** (`pkg/scheduler/apis/config/types.go`): Defines the `Plugins` struct and `PluginSet` for configuring which plugins run at each extension point
- **Framework Interface** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`): Local framework types
- **Metrics** (`pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go`): Metric constants for extension points

The answer.json file includes all relevant files, symbols (interfaces, structs, and types)

Unschedulable.\\n52: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n53: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ to\\n57: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n58: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n59: \\t// how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n68: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n69: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n70: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n71: \\t//\\n72: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n73: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n74: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n75: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n76: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n77: \\tWait\\n78: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n79: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n80: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n81: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n82: \\tSkip\\n83: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n84: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n85: \\t//\\n86: \\t// For example, if your plugin has to notify the scheduling result to an external component,\\n87: \\t// and wait for it to complete something **before** binding.\\n88: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n89: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n90: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n94: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n95: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n96: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n97: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n98: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n99: \\tPending\\n100: )\\n101: \\n102: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n103: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n104: \\n105: func (c Code) String() string {\\n106: \\treturn codes[c]\\n107: }\\n108: \\n109: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\\n110: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\\n111: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\\n112: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\\n113: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\\n114: type Status struct {\\n115: \\tcode    Code\\n116: \\treasons []string\\n117: \\terr     error\\n118: \\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\\n119: \\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\\n120: \\tplugin string\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\\n124: \\ts.err = err\\n125: \\treturn s\\n126: }\\n127: \\n128: // Code returns code of the Status.\\n129: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\\n130: \\tif s == nil {\\n131: \\t\\treturn Success\\n132: \\t}\\n133: \\treturn s.code\\n134: }\\n135: \\n136: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\\n137: func (s *Status) Message() string {\\n138: \\tif s == nil {\\n139: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n140: \\t}\\n141: \\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \\\", \\\")\\n142: }\\n143: \\n144: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\\n145: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\\n146: \\ts.plugin = plugin\\n147: }\\n148: \\n149: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\\n150: // and returns the given status object.\\n151: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\\n152: \\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\\n153: \\treturn s\\n154: }\\n155: \\n156: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\\n157: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\\n158: \\treturn s.plugin\\n159: }\\n160: \\n161: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\\n162: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\\n163: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n164: \\t\\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\\n165: \\t}\\n166: \\treturn s.reasons\\n167: }\\n168: \\n169: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\\n170: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\\n171: \\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\\n172: }\\n173: \\n174: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is nil or Code is \\\"Success\\\".\\n175: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\\n176: \\treturn s.Code() == Success\\n177: }\\n178: \\n179: // IsWait returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is non-nil and its Code is \\\"Wait\\\".\\n180: func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\\n181: \\treturn s.Code() == Wait\\n182: }\\n183: \\n184: // IsSkip returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is non-nil and its Code is \\\"Skip\\\".\\n185: func (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\\n186: \\treturn s.Code() == Skip\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: // IsRejected returns true if \\\"Status\\\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\\n190: func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\\n191: \\tcode := s.Code()\\n192: \\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\\n193: }\\n194: \\n195: // AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \\\"error\\\" object\\n196: // with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\\n197: func (s *Status) AsError() error {\\n198: \\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\\n199: \\t\\treturn nil\\n200: \\t}\\n201: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n202: \\t\\treturn s.err\\n203: \\t}\\n204: \\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\\n205: }\\n206: \\n207: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\\n208: // cmp.Equal.\\n209: func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\\n210: \\tif s == nil || x == nil {\\n211: \\t\\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\\n212: \\t}\\n213: \\tif s.code != x.code {\\n214: \\t\\treturn false\\n215: \\t}\\n216: \\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\\n217: \\t\\treturn false\\n218: \\t}\\n219: \\tif &Status{\\n232: \\t\\tcode:    code,\\n233: \\t\\treasons: reasons,\\n234: \\t}\\n235: \\treturn s\\n236: }\\n237: \\n238: // AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\\n239: func AsStatus(err error) }\\n280: \\n281: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\\n282: type PluginScore struct {\\n283: \\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\\n284: \\tName  string\\n285: \\tScore int64\\n286: }\\n287: \\n288: const (\\n289: \\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n290: \\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\\n291: \\n292: \\t// MinNodeScore \\n348: // PreFilterResult wraps needed info for scheduler framework to act upon PreFilter phase.\\n349: type PreFilterResult struct {\\n350: \\t// The set of nodes that should be considered \\n419: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"QueueSort\\\" plugins.\\n420: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Each event has a callback function that\\n449: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n450: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n451: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n452: \\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\\n453: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\\n454: \\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\\n455: \\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\\n456: \\t//\\n457: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n458: \\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\\n459: }\\n460: \\n461: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n462: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n463: // state.\\n464: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n465: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n466: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n467: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n468: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n469: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n470: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n471: }\\n472: \\n473: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n474: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n506: \\tPlugin\\n507: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n508: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n509: \\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n510: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n511: \\t//\\n512: \\t// \\\"Error\\\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\\n513: \\t//\\n514: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n515: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n516: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n517: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n518: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n519: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n520: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n521: \\t//\\n522: \\t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\\n523: \\t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\\n524: \\t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\\n525: \\t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. These plugins should\\n596: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\\n597: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\\n598: // rejection of the pod.\\n599: type ReservePlugin interface {\\n600: \\tPlugin\\n601: \\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\\n602: \\t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\\n603: \\t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\\n604: \\tReserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n605: \\t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\\n606: \\t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\\n607: \\t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\\n608: \\t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\\n609: \\t// method for the same plugin was not called.\\n610: \\tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n611: }\\n612: \\n613: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreBind\\\" plugins.\\n614: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\\n615: type PreBindPlugin interface {\\n616: \\tPlugin\\n617: \\t// PreBindPreFlight is called before PreBind, and the plugin is supposed to return two values:\\n618: \\t// - PreBindPreFlightResult (nil is valid, and means results with the zero values on all fields).\\n619: \\t// - Success, Skip, or Error status.\\n620: \\t// If it returns Success, it means this PreBind plugin will handle this pod.\\n621: \\t// If it returns Skip, it means this PreBind plugin has nothing to do with the pod, and PreBind will be skipped.\\n622: \\t// This function should be lightweight, and shouldn't do any actual operation, e.g., creating a volume etc.\\n623: \\tPreBindPreFlight(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*PreBindPreFlightResult, *Status)\\n624: \\n625: \\t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\\n626: \\t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\\n627: \\tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n628: }\\n629: \\n630: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PostBind\\\" plugins.\\n631: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\\n632: type PostBindPlugin interface {\\n633: \\tPlugin\\n634: \\t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\\n635: \\t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\\n636: \\t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\\n637: \\t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\\n638: \\tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n639: }\\n640: \\n641: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Permit\\\" plugins.\\n642: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\\n643: type PermitPlugin interface {\\n644: \\tPlugin\\n645: \\t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\\n646: \\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\\n647: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n648: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n649: \\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \\\"wait\\\", the framework will wait only\\n650: \\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\\n651: \\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\\n652: }\\n653: \\n654: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Bind\\\" plugins. Bind\\n655: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\\n656: type BindPlugin interface {\\n657: \\tPlugin\\n658: \\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\\n659: \\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\\n660: \\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\\n661: \\t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\\n662: \\t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\\n663: \\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\\n664: \\tBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: // A portion of a pod signature. The sign fragments from all plugins are combined\\n668: // together to create a unified signature.\\n669: type SignFragment struct {\\n670: \\t// Pod signature fragments are identified by a key, i.e., fragments with the same key\\n671: \\t// should contain the same value for the same pod. Plugin authors can return the same SignFragment\\n672: \\t// from multiple plugins, the framework just ignores duplicates. This allows plugins to share signers easily.\\n673: \\t//\\n674: \\t// Fragment names can be found in k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/signers.go. New fragment names for\\n675: \\t// in-tree plugins should be added there, and custom plugins can also use them.\\n676: \\t// Simple SignFragments which return a field should have names that follow the field name they return.\\n677: \\t// So a SignFragment that returns NodeName would have the key:\\n678: \\t//\\n679: \\t//\\t\\\"v1.Pod.Spec.NodeName\\\"\\n680: \\t//\\n681: \\t// If a SignFragment does some processing on the resource, its name should include the path to the base of the state it uses,\\n682: \\t// and then suffix this with a descriptive function name followed by (). So, for example, a SignFragment that only returns\\n683: \\t// Ephemeral volumes might use the key:\\n684: \\t//\\n685: \\t//\\t\\\"v1.Pod.Volumes.EphemeralVolumes()\\\"\\n686: \\tKey string\\n687: \\n688: \\t// The value of a SignFragment must be a json-marshallable object. Remember that we need to compare these across pods, so\\n689: \\t// plugins should ensure that lists where order doesn't matter are sorted, for example.\\n690: \\tValue any\\n691: }\\n692: \\n693: // The signature for a given pod after all of the results from plugins are consolidated.\\n694: type PodSignature []byte\\n695: \\n696: // SignPlugin is an interface that should be implemented by plugins that either filter or score\\n697: // pods to enable batching and gang scheduling optimizations.\\n698: // Each plugin returns SignFragments used to build a single signature per pod entering the scheduling cycle,\\n699: // and the scheduler uses signatures to determine whether it can use a cached scheduling result, or needs to\\n700: // recompute the prioritized nodes.\\n701: //\\n702: // If an enabled plugin that does Scoring, Prescoring, Filtering or Prefiltering does not implement this interface we will turn off batching for all pods.\\n703: type SignPlugin interface {\\n704: \\tPlugin\\n705: \\t// SignPod returns SignFragments for use in batching. This is called at every scheduling cycle\\n706: \\t// and is used to construct a signature builder used for pods. (KEP-5598).\\n707: \\t//\\n708: \\t// The sign fragments from all the plugins are combined to create a single signature. Only one fragment\\n709: \\t// with a given key will be included.\\n710: \\t//\\n711: \\t// Status means:\\n712: \\t//   - Success: the signer can sign the pod, accompanied by a set of signature fragments to be included.\\n713: \\t//   - Unschedulable: the signer refuses to sign the pod, meaning the pod is not eligible for opportunistic batching optimization.\\n714: \\t//   - Error: the signer hits something _unexpected_ and cannot build sign(s). A framework runtime just\\n715: \\t//     proceeds with scheduling this pod without opportunistic batching optimization like Unschedulable,\\n716: \\t//     but just report errors to logs.\\n717: \\tSignPod(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) ([]SignFragment, *Status)\\n718: }\\n719: \\n720: // Handle provides data and some tools that plugins can use. It is\\n721: // passed to the plugin factories at the time of plugin initialization. Plugins\\n722: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\\n723: type Handle interface {\\n724: \\t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n725: \\tPodNominator\\n726: \\t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\\n727: \\tPluginsRunner\\n728: \\t// PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\\n729: \\tPodActivator\\n730: \\t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. The snapshot\\n731: \\t// is taken at the beginning of a scheduling cycle and remains unchanged until\\n732: \\t// a pod finishes \\\"Permit\\\" point.\\n733: \\t//\\n734: \\t// It should be used only during scheduling cycle:\\n735: \\t// - There is no guarantee that the information remains unchanged in the binding phase of scheduling.\\n736: \\t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in the binding cycle (pre-bind/bind/post-bind/un-reserve plugin)\\n737: \\t//   otherwise, a concurrent read/write error might occur.\\n738: \\t// - There is no guarantee that the information is always up-to-date.\\n739: \\t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in QueueingHint and PreEnqueue\\n740: \\t//   otherwise, they might make a decision based on stale information.\\n741: \\t//\\n742: \\t// Instead, they should use the resources getting from Informer created from SharedInformerFactory().\\n743: \\tSnapshotSharedLister() SharedLister\\n744: \\n745: \\t// IterateOverWaitingPods acquires a read lock and iterates over the WaitingPods map.\\n746: \\tIterateOverWaitingPods(callback func(WaitingPod))\\n747: \\n748: \\t// GetWaitingPod returns a waiting pod given its UID.\\n749: \\tGetWaitingPod(uid types.UID) WaitingPod\\n750: \\n751: \\t// RejectWaitingPod rejects a waiting pod given its UID.\\n752: \\t// The return value indicates if the pod is waiting or not.\\n753: \\tRejectWaitingPod(uid types.UID) bool\\n754: \\n755: \\t// AddPodInPreBind adds a pod to the pods in preBind list.\\n756: \\tAddPodInPreBind(uid types.UID, cancel context.CancelCauseFunc)\\n757: \\n758: \\t// GetPodInPreBind returns a pod that is in the binding cycle but before it is bound given its UID.\\n759: \\tGetPodInPreBind(uid types.UID) PodInPreBind\\n760: \\n761: \\t// clientset.Interface\\n766: \\n767: \\t// KubeConfig returns the raw kube config.\\n768: \\tKubeConfig() *restclient.Config\\n769: \\n770: \\t// EventRecorder returns an event recorder.\\n771: \\tEventRecorder() events.EventRecorder\\n772: \\n773: \\tSharedInformerFactory() informers.SharedInformerFactory\\n774: \\n775: \\t// SharedDRAManager can be used to obtain DRA objects, and track modifications to them in-memory - mainly by the DRA plugin.\\n776: \\t// A non-default implementation can be plugged into the framework to simulate the state of DRA objects.\\n777: returns the profile name associated to a profile.\\n802: \\tProfileName() string\\n803: \\n804: \\t// WorkloadManager can be used to provide workload-aware scheduling.\\n805: \\tWorkloadManager() WorkloadManager\\n806: \\n807: \\t// Sign a pod.\\n808: \\tSignPod(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, recordPluginStats bool) PodSignature\\n809: }\\n810: \\n811: // Parallelizer helps run scheduling operations in parallel chunks where possible, to improve performance and CPU utilization.\\n812: type Parallelizer interface {\\n813: \\t// Until executes the given func doWorkPiece in parallel chunks, if applicable. Max number of chunks is param pieces.\\n814: \\tUntil(ctx context.Context, pieces int, doWorkPiece workqueue.DoWorkPieceFunc, operation string)\\n815: }\\n816: \\n817: // PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\\n818: type PodActivator interface {\\n819: \\t// Activate moves the given pods to activeQ.\\n820: \\t// If a pod isn't found in unschedulablePods or backoffQ and it's in-flight,\\n821: \\t// the wildcard event is registered so that the pod will be requeued when it comes back.\\n822: \\t// But, if a pod isn't found in unschedulablePods or backoffQ and it's not in-flight (i.e., completely unknown pod),\\n823: \\t// Activate would ignore the pod.\\n824: \\tActivate(logger klog.Logger, pods map[string]*v1.Pod)\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n828: type PodNominator interface {\\n829: \\t// AddNominatedPod adds the given pod to the nominator or\\n830: \\t// updates it if it already exists.\\n831: \\tAddNominatedPod(logger klog.Logger, pod PodInfo, nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo)\\n832: \\t// DeleteNominatedPodIfExists deletes nominatedPod from internal cache. governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // This file defines the scheduling framework plugin interfaces.\n18: \n19: package framework\n20: \n21: import (\n22: \t\"context\"\n23: \t\"errors\"\n24: \t\"math\"\n25: \t\"strings\"\n26: \t\"time\"\n27: \n28: \t\"github.com/google/go-cmp/cmp\"         //nolint:depguard\n29: \t\"github.com/google/go-cmp/cmp/cmpopts\" //nolint:depguard\n30: \tv1 \"k8s.io/api/core/v1\"\n31: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types\"\n32: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\"\n33: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/informers\"\n34: \tclientset \"k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes\"\n35: \trestclient \"k8s.io/client-go/rest\"\n36: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/events\"\n37: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue\"\n38: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n39: )\n40: \n41: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n42: type Code int\n43: \n44: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n45: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n46: const (\n47: \t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n48: \t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n49: \tSuccess Code = iota\n50: \t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n51: \t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n52: \t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n53: \t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n54: \tError\n55: \t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n56: \t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n57: \t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n58: \t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n59: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n60: \t//\n61: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n62: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n63: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n64: \tUnschedulable\n65: \t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n66: \t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n67: \t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n68: \t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n69: \t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n70: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n71: \t//\n72: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n73: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n74: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n75: \tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n76: \t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n77: \tWait\n78: \t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n79: \t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n80: \t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n81: \t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n82: \tSkip\n83: \t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n84: \t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n85: \t//\n86: \t// For example, if your plugin has to notify the scheduling result to an external component,\n87: \t// and wait for it to complete something **before** binding.\n88: \t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n89: \t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n90: \t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n91: \t//\n92: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n93: \t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n94: \t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n95: \t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n96: \t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n97: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n98: \t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n99: \tPending\n100: )\n101: \n102: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\n103: var codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n104: \n105: func (c Code) String() string {\n106: \treturn codes[c]\n107: }\n108: \n109: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n110: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n111: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n112: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n113: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\n114: type Status struct {\n115: \tcode    Code\n116: \treasons []string\n117: \terr     error\n118: \t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n119: \t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n120: \tplugin string\n121: }\n122: \n123: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n124: \ts.err = err\n125: \treturn s\n126: }\n127: \n128: // Code returns code of the Status.\n129: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\n130: \tif s == nil {\n131: \t\treturn Success\n132: \t}\n133: \treturn s.code\n134: }\n135: \n136: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n137: func (s *Status) Message() string {\n138: \tif s == nil {\n139: \t\treturn \"\"\n140: \t}\n141: \treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n142: }\n143: \n144: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\n145: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n146: \ts.plugin = plugin\n147: }\n148: \n149: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n150: // and returns the given status object.\n151: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n152: \ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n153: \treturn s\n154: }\n155: \n156: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\n157: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n158: \treturn s.plugin\n159: }\n160: \n161: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\n162: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n163: \tif s.err != nil {\n164: \t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n165: \t}\n166: \treturn s.reasons\n167: }\n168: \n169: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\n170: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n171: \ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n172: }\n173: \n174: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\n175: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n176: \treturn s.Code() == Success\n177: }\n178: \n179: // IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\n180: func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n181: \treturn s.Code() == Wait\n182: }\n183: \n184: // IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\n185: func (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n186: \treturn s.Code() == Skip\n187: }\n188: \n189: // IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\n190: func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n191: \tcode := s.Code()\n192: \treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n193: }\n194: \n195: // AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n196: // with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n197: func (s *Status) AsError() error {\n198: \tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n199: \t\treturn nil\n200: \t}\n201: \tif s.err != nil {\n202: \t\treturn s.err\n203: \t}\n204: \treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n205: }\n206: \n207: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n208: // cmp.Equal.\n209: func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n210: \tif s == nil || x == nil {\n211: \t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n212: \t}\n213: \tif s.code != x.code {\n214: \t\treturn false\n215: \t}\n216: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n217: \t\treturn false\n218: \t}\n219: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n220: \t\treturn false\n221: \t}\n222: \treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n223: }\n224: \n225: func (s *Status) String() string {\n226: \treturn s.Message()\n227: }\n228: \n229: // NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\n230: func NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n231: \ts := &Status{\n232: \t\tcode:    code,\n233: \t\treasons: reasons,\n234: \t}\n235: \treturn s\n236: }\n237: \n238: // AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\n239: func AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n240: \tif err == nil {\n241: \t\treturn nil\n242: \t}\n243: plugins.\n401: type Plugin interface {\n402: \tName() string\n403: }\n404: \n405: // PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n406: // These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ or backoffQ.\n407: // Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n408: // involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n409: // Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\n410: type PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n411: \tPlugin\n412: \t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ or backoffQ.\n413: \tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n414: }\n415: \n416: // LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\n417: type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 QueuedPodInfo) bool\n418: \n419: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n420: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n421: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\n422: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n423: \tPlugin\n424: \t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n425: \tLess(QueuedPodInfo, QueuedPodInfo) bool\n426: }\n427: \n428: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n429: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n430: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n431: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n432: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n433: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n434: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n435: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n436: //\n437: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) must implement this interface,\n438: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n439: //\n440: // Also, if EventsToRegister returns an empty list, that means the Pods failed by the plugin are not requeued by any events,\n441: // which doesn't make sense in most cases (very likely misuse)\n442: // since the pods rejected by the plugin could be stuck in the unschedulable pod pool forever.\n443: //\n444: // If plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n445: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n446: \tPlugin\n447: \t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n448: \t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n449: \t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n450: \t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n451: \t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n452: \t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n453: \t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n454: \t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n455: \t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n456: \t//\n457: \t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n458: \tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n459: }\n460: \n461: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n462: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n463: // state.\n464: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n465: \t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n466: \t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n467: \tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n468: \t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n469: \t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n470: \tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n471: }\n472: \n473: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n474: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins that implement PreFilterPlugin should\n475: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n476: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n477: \tPlugin\n478: \t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n479: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n480: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n481: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n482: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n483: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n484: \t//\n485: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n486: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n487: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodes []NodeInfo) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n488: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n489: \t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n490: \t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n491: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n492: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n493: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n494: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n495: }\n496: \n497: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n498: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n499: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n500: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n501: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n502: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n503: // running the pod. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\n506: \tPlugin\n507: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n508: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n509: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n510: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n511: \t//\n512: \t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n513: \t//\n514: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n515: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n516: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n517: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n518: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n519: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n520: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n521: \t//\n522: \t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\n523: \t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\n524: \t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\n525: \t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. For example, the\n526: \t// context gets canceled when a sufficient number of suitable\n527: \t// nodes have been found and searching for more isn't necessary\n528: \t// anymore.\n529: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n530: }\n531: \n532: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n533: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n534: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n535: \tPlugin\n536: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n537: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n538: \t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n539: \t//\n540: \t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n541: \t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n542: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n543: \t//\n544: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n545: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n546: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n547: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n548: \t//\n549: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n550: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n551: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n552: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n553: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n554: }\n555: \n556: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n559: // state or to generate logs/metrics. Plugins that implement PreScorePlugin should\n560: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n561: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n562: \tPlugin\n563: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n564: \t// passed the filtering phase. All scoring plugins must return success or\n586: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n587: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) (int64, *Status)\n588: \n589: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n590: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n591: }\n592: \n593: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n594: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n595: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n596: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n597: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n598: // rejection of the pod.\n599: type ReservePlugin interface {\n600: \tPlugin\n601: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n602: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n603: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n604: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n605: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n606: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n607: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n608: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n609: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n610: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n611: }\n612: \n613: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n614: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n615: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n616: \tPlugin\n617: \t// PreBindPreFlight is called before PreBind, and the plugin is supposed to return two values:\n618: \t// - PreBindPreFlightResult (nil is valid, and means results with the zero values on all fields).\n619: \t// - Success, Skip, or Error status.\n620: \t// If it returns Success, it means this PreBind plugin will handle this pod.\n621: \t// If it returns Skip, it means this PreBind plugin has nothing to do with the pod, and PreBind will be skipped.\n622: \t// This function should be lightweight, and shouldn't do any actual operation, e.g., creating a volume etc.\n623: \tPreBindPreFlight(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*PreBindPreFlightResult, *Status)\n624: \n625: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n626: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n627: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n628: }\n629: \n630: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n631: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n632: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n633: \tPlugin\n634: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n635: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n636: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n637: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n638: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n639: }\n640: \n641: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n642: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n643: type PermitPlugin interface {\n644: \tPlugin\n645: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n646: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n647: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n648: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n649: \t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n650: \t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n651: \tPermit(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n652: }\n653: \n654: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n655: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n656: type BindPlugin interface {\n657: \tPlugin\n658: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n659: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n660: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n661: \t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n662: \t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n663: \t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n664: \tBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n665: }\n666: \n667: // A portion of a pod signature. The sign fragments from all plugins are combined\n668: // together to create a unified signature.\n669: type SignFragment struct {\n670: \t// Pod signature fragments are identified by a key, i.e., fragments with the same key\n671: \t// should contain the same value for the same pod. Plugin authors can return the same SignFragment\n672: \t// from multiple plugins, the framework just ignores duplicates. This allows plugins to share signers easily.\n673: \t//\n674: \t// Fragment names can be found in k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/signers.go. New fragment names for\n675: \t// in-tree plugins should be added there, and custom plugins can also use them.\n676: \t// Simple SignFragments which return a field should have names that follow the field name they return.\n677: \t// So a SignFragment that returns NodeName would have the key:\n678: \t//\n679: \t//\t\"v1.Pod.Spec.NodeName\"\n680: \t//\n681: \t// If a SignFragment does some processing on the resource, its name should include the path to the base of the state it uses,\n682: \t// and then suffix this with a descriptive function name followed by (). So, for example, a SignFragment that only returns\n683: \t// Ephemeral volumes might use the key:\n684: \t//\n685: \t//\t\"v1.Pod.Volumes.EphemeralVolumes()\"\n686: \tKey string\n687: \n688: \t// The value of a SignFragment must be a json-marshallable object. Remember that we need to compare these across pods, so\n689: \t// plugins should ensure that lists where order doesn't matter are sorted, for example.\n690: \tValue any\n691: }\n692: \n693: // The signature for a given pod after all of the results from plugins are consolidated.\n694: type PodSignature []byte\n695: \n696: // SignPlugin is an interface that should be implemented by plugins that either filter or score\n697: // pods to enable batching and gang scheduling optimizations.\n698: // Each plugin returns SignFragments used to build a single signature per pod entering the scheduling cycle,\n699: // and the scheduler uses signatures to determine whether it can use a cached scheduling result, or needs to\n700: // recompute the prioritized nodes.\n701: //\n702: // If an enabled plugin that does Scoring, Prescoring, Filtering or Prefiltering does not implement this interface we will turn off batching for all pods.\n703: type SignPlugin interface {\n704: \tPlugin\n705: \t// SignPod returns SignFragments for use in batching. This is called at every scheduling cycle\n706: \t// and is used to construct a signature builder used for pods. (KEP-5598).\n707: \t//\n708: \t// The sign fragments from all the plugins are combined to create a single signature. Only one fragment\n709: \t// with a given key will be included.\n710: \t//\n711: \t// Status means:\n712: \t//   - Success: the signer can sign the pod, accompanied by a set of signature fragments to be included.\n713: \t//   - Unschedulable: the signer refuses to sign the pod, meaning the pod is not eligible for opportunistic batching optimization.\n714: \t//   - Error: the signer hits something _unexpected_ and cannot build sign(s). A framework runtime just\n715: \t//     proceeds with scheduling this pod without opportunistic batching optimization like Unschedulable,\n716: \t//     but just report errors to logs.\n717: \tSignPod(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) ([]SignFragment, *Status)\n718: }\n719: \n720: // Handle provides data and some tools that plugins can use. It is\n721: // passed to the plugin factories at the time of plugin initialization. scheduling cycle:\n735: \t// - There is no guarantee that the information remains unchanged in the binding phase of scheduling.\n736: \t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in the binding cycle If they need to\n137: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\n138: type Plugins struct {\n139: \t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\n140: \tPreEnqueue PluginSet\n141: \n142: \t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\n143: \tQueueSort PluginSet\n144: \n145: \t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"PreFilter\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n146: \tPreFilter PluginSet\n147: \n148: \t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\n149: \tFilter PluginSet\n150: \n151: \t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\n152: \tPostFilter PluginSet\n153: \n154: \t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\n155: \tPreScore PluginSet\n156: \n157: \t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\n158: \tScore PluginSet\n159: \n160: \t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\n161: \t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\n162: \tReserve PluginSet\n163: \n164: \t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\n165: \tPermit PluginSet\n166: \n167: \t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\n168: \tPreBind PluginSet\n169: \n170: \t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \"Bind\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\n171: \t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\n172: \tBind PluginSet\n173: \n174: \t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\n175: \tPostBind PluginSet\n176: \n177: \t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\n178: \tMultiPoint PluginSet\n179: }\n180: \n181: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\n182: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\n183: type PluginSet struct {\n184: \t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\n185: \t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\n186: \tEnabled []Plugin\n187: \t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\n188: \t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \"*\" should be provided.\n189: \tDisabled []Plugin\n190: }\n191: \n192: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n202: // It is up to the plugin to process these Args.\n203: type PluginConfig struct {\n204: \t// Name defines the name of plugin being configured\n205: \tName string\n206: \t// Args defines the arguments passed to the plugins at the time of initialization. Args can have arbitrary structure.\n207: \tArgs runtime.Object\n208: }\n209: \n210: /*\n211:  * NOTE: The following variables and methods are intentionally left out of the staging mirror.\n212:  */\n213: const (\n214: \t// DefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore defines the percentage of nodes of all nodes\n215: \t// that once found feasible, the scheduler stops looking for more nodes.\n216: \t// A value of 0 means adaptive, meaning the scheduler figures out a proper default.\n217: \tDefaultPercentageOfNodesToScore = 0\n218: \n219: \t// MaxCustomPriorityScore is the max score UtilizationShapePoint expects.\n220: \tMaxCustomPriorityScore int64 = 10\n221: \n222: \t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n223: \tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n224: \n225: \t// MaxWeight defines the max weight value allowed for custom PriorityPolicy\n226: \tMaxWeight = MaxTotalScore / MaxCustomPriorityScore\n227: )\n228: \n229: // Names returns the list of enabled plugin names.\n230: func (p *Plugins) Names() []string {\n231: ",

through Go interfaces located primarily in staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/interface.go, which serves as the public API. These extension points are: PreFilter (PreFilterPlugin), Filter (FilterPlugin), PostFilter (PostFilterPlugin), PreScore (PreScorePlugin), Score (ScorePlugin), Reserve (ReservePlugin), PreBind (PreBindPlugin), Bind (BindPlugin), and PostBind (PostBindPlugin). All these interfaces embed the base Plugin interface which requires a Name() method. Supporting interfaces include PreFilterExtensions (for incremental AddPod/RemovePod operations), ScoreExtensions (for NormalizeScore operations), EnqueueExtensions (for efficient pod queue management), and SignPlugin (for batching optimizations). The framework implementation is in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go, which contains the frameworkImpl struct that maintains plugin slices for each extension point and provides Run* methods to execute them: RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunPreScorePlugins, RunScorePlugins, RunReservePluginsReserve/Unreserve, RunPermitPlugins, RunPreBindPlugins, RunPreBindPreFlights, RunBindPlugins, and RunPostBindPlugins. The extensionPoint struct in framework.go groups plugin configuration and implementation slices, while getExtensionPoints method returns all nine extension points in order. Plugin registration is managed through the Registry type (a map of PluginFactory functions) defined in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go. Plugin configuration is defined in pkg/scheduler/apis/config/types.go via the Plugins struct which contains PluginSet fields for each extension point, and versioned configuration types are in pkg/scheduler/apis/config/v1/types.go. The pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go file provides local framework types and the pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go file defines metrics constants for each extension point.\"\n}\n",

Supporting interfaces include PreFilterExtensions (for incremental AddPod/RemovePod operations), ScoreExtensions (for NormalizeScore operations), EnqueueExtensions (for efficient pod queue management), and SignPlugin (for batching optimizations). The framework implementation is in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go, which contains the frameworkImpl struct that maintains plugin slices for each extension point and provides Run* methods to execute them: RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunPreScorePlugins, RunScorePlugins, RunReservePluginsReserve/Unreserve, RunPermitPlugins, RunPreBindPlugins, RunPreBindPreFlights, RunBindPlugins, and RunPostBindPlugins. The extensionPoint struct in framework.go groups plugin configuration and implementation slices, while getExtensionPoints method returns all nine extension points in order. Plugin registration is managed through the Registry type (a map of PluginFactory functions) defined in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go. Plugin configuration is defined in pkg/scheduler/apis/config/types.go via the Plugins struct which contains PluginSet fields for each extension point, and versioned configuration types are in pkg/scheduler/apis/config/v1/types.go. The pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go file provides local framework types and the pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go file defines metrics constants for each extension point.\"\n}\n",
